  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer3924739668779733057">'Happy fifty-third birthday, Doctor. Welcome to the first day of your death. You ruined my life. And now I fully intend to ruin yours.<br/><br/>'You have exactly one fortnight, starting tomorrow morning at 6 a.m., to discover who I am.   <span id="freeText3924739668779733057" style="display:none">'Happy fifty-third birthday, Doctor. Welcome to the first day of your death. You ruined my life. And now I fully intend to ruin yours.<br /><br />'You have exactly one fortnight, starting tomorrow morning at 6 a.m., to discover who I am. When you succeed you must purchase one of those tiny ads at the bottom of the New York Times front page, and print my name there.<br /><br />'If you do not succeed, then ... you will take note that the second sheet of this letter contains the names of fifty-two of your relatives. If you are unable to purchase the ad as described, then you will have this choice: kill yourself immediately or I will destroy one of these innocent people.'<br /><br />Until the moment he opens the letter, New York psychologist Dr Frederick Starks has led a quiet and, so he believes, blameless life. He has no idea why he's being judged by this unknown tormentor a former patient - who then lethally begins to demonstrate the potential of his, or her, threats. As the layers of Starks's carefully constructed life are stripped from him, he quickly finds himself a powerless pawn in a psychopath's devious game of vengeance.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">In my opinion. Although it took me too long to finish it (because of my reading level), I absolutely loved it. The characters are unpredictable and th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">In my opinion. Although it took me too long to finish it (because of my reading level), I absolutely loved it. The characters are unpredictable and they appear in the story in the most appropriate moment wich gives life to the plot. <br />I'd recommend you to read "The Analyst" if you are that kind of person who enjoys trying to discover who is involved in the crime, who is lying and who's not. This novel is a masterpiece in which you need to have all your senses on. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2524219295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2524219295" />
    <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda"><img alt="Arah-Lynda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601299926p2/5859453.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2524219295?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arah-Lynda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arah-Lynda" href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda">Arah-Lynda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5859453-arah-lynda?shelf=i-said">i-said</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2524219295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10112905694411521124">Reading this took me back to the days of my youth. Perhaps you remember those days. The early days of marriage, young children, shaky foundations, isolated locations, a love of reading but limited choices. Whatever, you paint the picture. I remember reading a book and attempting to cook dinner at the same time. Suddenly I became aware that my husband was in the kitchen and the potatoes were burning. Trust me there was little to salvage from that “meal”. <br/><br/>This book that I read is a mass market pap</span>
  <span id="freeText10112905694411521124" style="display:none">Reading this took me back to the days of my youth. Perhaps you remember those days. The early days of marriage, young children, shaky foundations, isolated locations, a love of reading but limited choices. Whatever, you paint the picture. I remember reading a book and attempting to cook dinner at the same time. Suddenly I became aware that my husband was in the kitchen and the potatoes were burning. Trust me there was little to salvage from that “meal”. <br /><br />This book that I read is a mass market paperback, my least favourite vehicle for the written word, and came to me as recommended and gratis from my youngest daughter’s, mother in law, a voracious reader. That aside, honestly, when given a choice, I cannot see myself picking this one up. <br /><br />Still there is a good story here and even though it took me a while to warm up to the protagonist, the game was definitely afoot. Ricky, a psychoanalyst, is given fifteen days to identify his stalker or kill himself. The stakes are high and measured in human lives. If you think this is a hoax or a joke stay tuned and allow Katzenbach to convince you otherwise. <br /><br />Honestly for me, the writing was something of a workout. Too many words became a recurring refrain within the confines of my read. Still a picture was indeed painted and I became invested in the outcome. The story took over and I rode out the waves. Words and all. <br /><br />Find yourself a comfy perch and settle in. You are going to be a while.<br /><br />It was an enjoyable ride. 3.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10112905694411521124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1058753030?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="José" class="user" itemprop="url" name="José" href="/user/show/35062854-jos">José</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35062854-jos?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1058753030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8196878245597675704">Reseña en español de <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49392.El_psicoanalista' title='El psicoanalista by John Katzenbach' rel='nofollow noopener'>El psicoanalista</a> en el blog: <a href='http://rincondellectorconstante.blogspot.com.uy/2015/09/el-psicoanalista-john-katzenbach.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Click aquí</a><br/><br/>This was the first Katzenbach book I read and it was really good. I never heard of this author prior reading this novel but it was a birthday present and the premise looked really interesting: a psychopath who calls himself Rumpelstiltskin, threats doctor Frederick Starks saying that he has to figure out his identity in 15 days or he will kill somebody from the doctor's family. The only way to stop Rumpelstiltskin from killing is to win</span>
  <span id="freeText8196878245597675704" style="display:none">Reseña en español de <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49392.El_psicoanalista" title="El psicoanalista by John Katzenbach" rel="nofollow noopener">El psicoanalista</a> en el blog: <a href="http://rincondellectorconstante.blogspot.com.uy/2015/09/el-psicoanalista-john-katzenbach.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Click aquí</a><br /><br />This was the first Katzenbach book I read and it was really good. I never heard of this author prior reading this novel but it was a birthday present and the premise looked really interesting: a psychopath who calls himself Rumpelstiltskin, threats doctor Frederick Starks saying that he has to figure out his identity in 15 days or he will kill somebody from the doctor's family. The only way to stop Rumpelstiltskin from killing is to win the game or that the doctor commits suicide.<br /><br />It was a great read. The book is fast paced with lots of mysteries and nice plot twists that kept me reading non stop, towards the half it slows down a little bit but luckily Katzenbach quickly picks up the frantic rhythm of the first chapters reaching a very good ending.<br />Even though I sort of figured out who Rumpelstiltskin was before finishing, it didn't stopped me from enjoying this book because what really interested me was to know if the doctor could survive this wicked game.<br />Another thing I really liked is how the author describes the psyche of the different characters and the deeper implications of the game planned by Rumpelstiltskin, also the villain was great because of his determination to destroy doctor Starks's life.<br /><br />With this kind of books I always have the concern that the ending can be stupid or far fetched, fortunately this wasn't the case. Without being a mind-blowing ending (at least for me) I found it to be satisfactory and it wrapped up the book perfectly.<br /><br /><b>So, if you're looking for a fast and exciting psychological thriller this book can be good for you. I breezed through the second half desperate to know how the story would end and it didn't disappoint me. I'll definitely read more books by this author in the future.</b></span>

<div id="review_2919636633" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Fonch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8647009-fonch"><img alt="Fonch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333994582p2/8647009.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14337353954638408786">Ladies and gentlemen after writing the review of Dorothy Dunett's"Game of Kings" <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2989041800?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1'>https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> <br/>penetrated a negative dynamic of readings. Actually, this book I took out of the attic last year, but I didn't get a chance to read it, because the heathen knew a truth that Cronus was a relentless deity, and it was upon me.   <span id="freeText14337353954638408786" style="display:none">Ladies and gentlemen after writing the review of Dorothy Dunett's"Game of Kings" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2989041800?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> <br />penetrated a negative dynamic of readings. Dunett's book was followed by that of John Katzenbach. Actually, this book I took out of the attic last year, but I didn't get a chance to read it, because the heathen knew a truth that Cronus was a relentless deity, and it was upon me. The plot of the book seemed very interesting, and I was very familiar with Katzenbach because I saw several adaptations of his novels on my home TV. I mean"Just Cause" a very politically incorrect novel about the death penalty, and racism (at least the film) had a particularity, which is that it doesn't matter the race or sex of a person. This one can always be bad. There is no beneficial genre, and another evil genre as advocated by certain ideologies, and certain lobbyists, nor a better race than the others. White supremacism has been abandoned, to reach a crossroads just as wrong as Edward Said's <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16770310.Edward_W_Said">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> <br />, who blames the white male for all the evils of mankind. Katzenbach's novel had the courage to debunk those demagogue groupers, which Tom Wolfe also satirized <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3083854.Tom_Wolfe">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> also has a certain touch of the"Cape of Fear " <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/434229.Cape_Fear?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4...</a> that served as a backdrop for two interesting film adaptations directed by J. L. Thompson, and Martin Scorsese and starring Gregory Peck, and Robert Mitchum and in the Scorsese version starred Nick Nolte, Robert de Niro, and Juliette Lewis playing lolita. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Fear_(1962_film)">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Fe...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Fear_(1991_film)">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Fe...</a> <br />His second novel I had the pleasure of seeing I also really liked"The War of Hart" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/148841.Hart_s_War?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> where a soldier played by Colin Farrell, was to defend a prisoner from a concentration camp, accused of killing another played by the ever-solvent Linus Roache, who was the snitch of the Nazis, the Polonium, Chesty would have called him the rat :-) <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7014283.G_K_Chesterton">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> and apart from that the film witnessed the confrontation between the Nazi camp general, and the intrepid prisoner chief played by Bruce Willis, I also liked to have a touch to the a wonderful traitor in Hell by Billy Wilder, and who allowed him in a well-deserved way to win the only Oscar of his career to William Holden <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film620366.html">https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film6...</a> So this first novel I was going to read to John Katzenbach was going to read it with great anticipation. But as my grandmother said by paternal line " I don't want to see my children with happy beginnings" and that has been the flaw in John Katzenbach's novel. It started very well, in fact, the proposal reminded me of Calvary <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film858609.html">https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film8...</a> both have something in common a priest, in this case a psychiatrist (Starks) who have made a mistake with a patient. In the case of Calvary a parishioner who has been abused by a priest, and who takes it with poor Brendan Glesson, which the only thing he has in common with the sexual aggressor is that he is also a priest. This novel in which the villain adopts an alias in this case that of the cruel Rumpelstiltskin. There's something my sister tells me about this. Most German romantics apart from moralists had a virtue were religious, and their tales had a moral tone, and they adopted that language to teach truths to children, although it is usually adults who read these stories. I don't know if Katzenbach will know this, though it is possible that he does, when a man loses his reflection, or his shadow is actually losing his soul. What is Rumpelstiltskin really? It's the devil. It was a way of representing the demon, and I believe, this character with a purpose. Preventing children from engaging in witchcraft or making pacts with the demon <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2938140.Jacob_Grimm">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2938141.Wilhelm_Grimm">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> because Faust's shadow <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/406373.Faust?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18525.Dr_Faustus?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> was rooted in the Teutonic country. So it doesn't seem far-fetched to me, that Katzenbach gave his psychopath Rumpelstiltskin's nickname and his henchmen Merlin's, or Virgil. The first part seemed good, or very good, if Katzenbach had finished it like this, i would certainly have given it three, or maybe four stars, though I think, it was a lot. The first part shows how a person's life can be destroyed. With how easily man thinks he's at the top, and he thinks he's untouchable. That's what happens to Starks' widower, who has a hard time assimilating, with whom he's playing it. This cat-and-mouse game reminds me a lot of the one played by Simon Gruber/Jeremy Irons with John MacLane/Bruce Willis (I am very skeptical about the subject of psychiatry, but Hollywood does believe in it so in this case the psychiatrist totally hits despite the McGuffin of Fort Knox) <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film971189.html">https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film9...</a> I must admit that I liked the four more, but The Jungle of Crystal 3 revenge fits more into Mr. Katzenbach's novel. The game Rumpelstiltskin and Starks play in is brutal and unalled. Stripping him of everything ruins his reputation, attacks his loved ones, takes away his money. What happens to Starks could happen to any of us. So you have to take the lead a drastic measure. The problem is that the second part is where I have suffered the greatest disappointment. It's not just that I liked it less. The problem is, I didn't believe her. I see it easier for a psychopath to emerge and sink you, that a person like the phoenix can rise from the ashes. Starting from scratch is very difficult, and very complicated. Besides, everything that happens becomes strange, and surreal. The worst thing that can happen in a novel is that you don't believe in it, and that's what happened to me with the second part of the Psychoanalyst. ". Moreover, a tremendous chasm of Katzenbach has been found, and it is the chasm that exists between Europe, and the United States. He considered a lot of things in Europe. Among them is the fascination, which Europe seems to have for self-destruction and accepting ideologies, and philosophical postulates more destructive than the previous ones. Proof of the decline in which we live apart from the demographic winter, and the ageing population by following those policies, and those sobiding intellectuals, which I reject. It is the raking secularism, and the forms of intellectualism, and atheism that afflict us. However, there is one thing that, if I believe, that Europe is right, and the United States is not. It is that I cannot approve of Ricky Starks' behavior that he seems to return as a kind of modern Count of Monte Cristo, despite the advice of the Abat of Faria trying to dissuade Edmond Dantes before from his desires for vengeance <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7126.The_Count_of_Monte_Cristo?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7...</a> It is true that I may not have reached some rejectable extremes, but in my opinion there are worse things than death, and I think in part the evil triad has won, because it has succeeding in paraphrasing Nietszche (I apologise to Peter Marbury <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44686251-el-sr-marbury?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4...</a> ) becomes a monster, just like the enemies he faces. I don't agree that the end Starks gives to his enemies is the fairest. I said one thing. Everyone knows that Alejandro Dumas wrote "The Count of Monte Cristo", but it is quite possible that people do not know that he wrote a second part called "The Hand of the Dead" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4717814-la-mano-del-muerto?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4717814-la-mano-del-muerto?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4...</a> curiously edited by a Catholic publishing house in my country. From what I see in Goodreads, maybe not so popular. But it may be because he tells us the consequences of revenge. The problem with revenge is that it has no end, with every act of retaliation the hatred increases, and conflicts last for generations, or centuries. That is why I am with G.K. Chesterton (we recommend the case of the "arrow of heaven" in the "Incredulityof Father Brown" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/184594.The_Incredulity_of_Father_Brown?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> ) that one must trust more in the laws, to despite his mistakes, that in revenge. Precisely the suppression of the Faidhe was the great achievement of the late Middle Ages, and the one that allowed the kings to move to the Modern Age, and build the modern states today . Interestingly, this reminiscent of the law of thaion, and of the eye for an eye is one of the consequences of the Reformation. In this case of Calvinism. So such behavior of Starks must be rejected. This brilliant reflection was made by the writer Miyuki Miyabe in her novel "Crossfire" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/123556.Crossfire?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> that is the denunciation made by the author of a vigilante, who in the end crosses the boundaries, and is becomes a murderer, just like the killers she kills (another example of this is the film Exemplary Citizen with Gerard Butler, and Jaimie Foxx <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film565861.html">https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film5...</a> , as we talk about the Crystal Jungle 3 A Revenge the end that is He was scheduled to do to Simon Gruber instead of going in the helicopter with Zeus Carver/Samuel L. Jackson. Partly because of our individualism we feel a fascination, because the character falls , and move to the dark side. I must give the only fool, but it seems to me a very petty and impoverishing enjoyment.I don't think it's right to imitate the examples of Hamlet, Charles Bronson, or Liam Nesson. I believe that this unethical behavior of Starks is going to have consequences, and it seems to give me the reason John Katzenbach, since he has written a sequel to this novel. It's not the only novel this summer to have incurred this ruling. P.N. Elrod made the same mistake in his 1930s vampiric saga <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/609101.Lifebloo">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6...</a> d Anyway if I must admit, that the second part of the novel is much worse, hence this rating. I hope John Katzenbach has more luck with my ratings in the future. My next review should be Drive by James Sallis <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/176378.Drive?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14337353954638408786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText120625696546995260" style="display:none">This book was one of the most interesting reads I've had the pleasure to experience. The plot, details, scenery, descriptions, characters, surroundings, the smoothly developed plot, and the amazing complexity of it all were a definite masterpiece. I kept reading, my eyes anxiously and nervously glued to the pages, expecting, and guessing, and guessing again, but things were never as I expected, and I was easily captured by the feelings and situations the main character was in. <br /><br />The first part of the book I was constantly nervous, stressed, frustrated, anxious, expecting... I was angry, sad, and flabbergasted by the tense happenings in the story.<br /><br />The second part of the book was enjoyable. Much more dramatic, yet systematically chilling at the same time. <br /><br />I loved how the author kept us guessing who Rumpelstiltskin was, and until just the very last moment he let us know. I am greatly impressed with the ingenious creation of this writer, and I definitely will keep this book stored in my memory whenever someone asks me for an amazing psychological thriller. I loved it. 5 huge stars. </span>

  <span id="freeText1899838216084077576" style="display:none">The Analyst- Ex<br />John Katzenbach<br />New York City psychoanalyst Frederick (Ricky) Starks receives an anonymous missive saying that Starks has ruined the writer's life and that he has ten days in which to discover his or her identity. If he fails, he must commit suicide; if he does not comply with this order, someone in his family will suffer or die. At first Ricky is disoriented and unable to function effectively, but he soon begins to take action. Using his research skills, he finds that a former patient was so despondent that she killed herself, leaving three children as orphans. But this information is not enough to save Ricky's life. Thus, he goes on a journey of self-discovery, calling upon unknown depths of endurance and using his medical training in order to survive.<br /><br />2002 Top Ten - psychological suspense, intriguing and wonderfully written.</span>

<div id="review_91865258" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91865258" />
    <a title="Mimi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2690037-mimi"><img alt="Mimi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545519869p2/2690037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91865258?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi" href="/user/show/2690037-mimi">Mimi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345426277" href="/book/show/1564303.The_Analyst">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91865258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16342540704025681114">Remember that somewhat twisted fairy tale known as Rumpelstiltskin? You know, it starts when a poor miller tells the King that he has a daughter who can turn straw into gold. The greedy King decides to put this to the test and gives the maiden until morning to spin a room full of straw into gold – if she is unable to do so, she will die. Hopeless in her task, the maiden is surprised when a troll-like man enters her tower and offers to help her. …With a price of course! After she gives the troll </span>
  <span id="freeText16342540704025681114" style="display:none">Remember that somewhat twisted fairy tale known as Rumpelstiltskin? You know, it starts when a poor miller tells the King that he has a daughter who can turn straw into gold. The greedy King decides to put this to the test and gives the maiden until morning to spin a room full of straw into gold – if she is unable to do so, she will die. Hopeless in her task, the maiden is surprised when a troll-like man enters her tower and offers to help her. …With a price of course! After she gives the troll all her material possessions, she is forced to offer him her first child once she becomes Queen. Of course, once her son was born, she did not want to give him up. So the troll gave her 3 days to guess his name – if she did this, she would be able to keep her baby. By some stroke of luck, the Queen’s messenger came across the troll dancing in front of a bonfire, gloating that his name indeed was Rumpelstiltskin. Thus the Queen was able to keep her baby. <br /><br />Dr. Frederick Starks’ also had to discover the identity of a Rumpelstiltskin, but his path was paved with many more difficulties than was that of the Queen. Frederick Starks (“Ricky”), is a psychoanalyst who is thrust into a nightmarish version of this fairy tale when he receives a letter basically saying that if he doesn’t discover the identity of the letter-writer within 15 days, he will have to commit suicide. If he doesn’t commit suicide, one of 52 family members whose names are included in the list will be tormented, ruined or killed. Over the course of the next 15 days, Rumpelstiltskin proves the seriousness of his threat by systematically ruining Ricky financially and professionally. <br /><br />Despite the fact the story was probably a bit longer than necessary (overdone description is some parts), this well-crafted and suspenseful story has more twists and turns than one can imagine and the game that Ricky is forced to play is both frustrating and intriguing. Thought provoking social commentary is made throughout the book, touching on topics such as inadequate medical care, homelessness, Internet fraud and false identities. I also appreciated how Mr. Katzenbach referenced other literature, especially the works of Homer as well as Greek mythology (not to forget the Brothers Grimm!) <br /><br />This would translate really well on the big screen, just as Hart’s War did! Although I am having a hard time casting Ricky Starks – Bruce Willis and John Travolta crossed my mind but I’m just not sure! Mr. Katzenbach and his producers will have to surprise us!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16342540704025681114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer9657537977730079000">A TERRIFIC SPELLBINFING READ<br/>I can place "The Analyst" in the list of those precious books I will never forget <br/><br/>It is a terrific psico-thriller with a creepy tint, the intensity of a blockbuster every step of the way and the power to get deep enough to probe the functioning of the deep recesses of the human mind <br/><br/>It is so well written that you can perceive rather than learn the different array of emotions exuded by his main dynamic character throughout all the pages from beginning to end, and for m</span>
  <span id="freeText9657537977730079000" style="display:none">A TERRIFIC SPELLBINFING READ<br />I can place "The Analyst" in the list of those precious books I will never forget <br /><br />It is a terrific psico-thriller with a creepy tint, the intensity of a blockbuster every step of the way and the power to get deep enough to probe the functioning of the deep recesses of the human mind <br /><br />It is so well written that you can perceive rather than learn the different array of emotions exuded by his main dynamic character throughout all the pages from beginning to end, and for me this is the feature that sets its apart from the pack <br /><br />The main topic is original, and the structure of the plot too, depicting with a psychological view how an individual identity life, career and reputation is destroyed and how in turn he can rise from the ashes and exact his revenge to finally get even with those who can conspired to destroy him, using only his intelligence and education as his main resource, to plan strategies with designated steps and succeed battling in a hostile, tough, world <br /><br />The ending, dissapointing in many thrillers of this kind, (whodunnit), is very well solved and in line with the quality of the whole book (rumplestilskin, the bad guy is finally unmasked) <br /><br />This book invites to try other works of Mr Katzenbach, something I will surely do shortly <br /><br />As I said at the beginning I will put this book in my amazon listmania list, because I loved it <br /><br />Great job </span>
  <a data-text-id="9657537977730079000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer209357630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5120170468886148241">The best-selling author or Hart's War did not disappoint with THE ANALYST. I felt as alone, helpless and solitary as the protagonist as he advanced further into the terror of a very real cat and mouse game. Dr. Starks, a professional psychoanalyst, receives a threatening letter from a Mr. "Rumplestiltskin" demanding that he guess his real name within 15 days. If the good doctor does not guess or guesses incorrectly, Mr. R. will start killing off the doctor's relatives. Mr. R. will let the doctor</span>
  <span id="freeText5120170468886148241" style="display:none">The best-selling author or Hart's War did not disappoint with THE ANALYST. I felt as alone, helpless and solitary as the protagonist as he advanced further into the terror of a very real cat and mouse game. Dr. Starks, a professional psychoanalyst, receives a threatening letter from a Mr. "Rumplestiltskin" demanding that he guess his real name within 15 days. If the good doctor does not guess or guesses incorrectly, Mr. R. will start killing off the doctor's relatives. Mr. R. will let the doctor out of the game if Starks just kills himself. As the game begins Mr. R. destroys the doctor's life bit by bit, financially, professionally, socially and so on. There is no one the man can turn to. <br />Every time I thought of some way out, so would the hero . . . and then a brick wall would appear. Mr. R. is always several steps ahead as he seeks revenge for a mistake the doctor made 20 years prior. <br />Everything seems utterly hopeless until the doctor resigns himself to death. And then . . .<br />Excellent read - highly recommended. I'm off to look for more of John Katzenbach's works.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5120170468886148241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16928300619532657823">it's a good story, and the weak main character actually shows some growth toward the end of the book. For a book that analyzes everything, the ending felt rushed with little insight. <br/><br/>The real identity of Rumpelstiltskin is not too hard to decipher, there aren't that many characters in the book to suspect, so his revelation is fairly predictable.   <span id="freeText16928300619532657823" style="display:none">it's a good story, and the weak main character actually shows some growth toward the end of the book. However, there is a lot of "psycho-babble" that gets a little old. For a book that analyzes everything, the ending felt rushed with little insight. <br /><br />The real identity of Rumpelstiltskin is not too hard to decipher, there aren't that many characters in the book to suspect, so his revelation is fairly predictable. However, some of the other surprises are nifty and add to the suspense.<br /><br />The ending is a little disappointing in that we never really know what happens to Rumpelstiltskin.<br />All in all, though, a good read.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1890635486" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1890635486" />
    <a title="Belén" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7470972-bel-n"><img alt="Belén" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547304140p2/7470972.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_1035215049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1035215049" />
    <a title="Tanja Berg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5935491-tanja-berg"><img alt="Tanja Berg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558953813p2/5935491.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1035215049?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanja Berg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanja Berg" href="/user/show/5935491-tanja-berg">Tanja Berg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345426277" href="/book/show/1564303.The_Analyst">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5935491-tanja-berg?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1035215049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5332853473489511713">This was a highly entertaining thriller that completely fulfilled my expectations. Dr. Frederick Starks, a psychoanalyst, is contacted by someone who calls himself Rumplestiltskin. He gets 15 days to find out the real name of Mr. R. After the deadline has passed he either has to kill himself or something terrible will befall one of Starks' relatives. The reason for this race against death is, of course, revenge. Mr. R allows Starks to ask him questions through the Times' personal ads section. He</span>
  <span id="freeText5332853473489511713" style="display:none">This was a highly entertaining thriller that completely fulfilled my expectations. Dr. Frederick Starks, a psychoanalyst, is contacted by someone who calls himself Rumplestiltskin. He gets 15 days to find out the real name of Mr. R. After the deadline has passed he either has to kill himself or something terrible will befall one of Starks' relatives. The reason for this race against death is, of course, revenge. Mr. R allows Starks to ask him questions through the Times' personal ads section. He begins to try to find out what he has done - or failed to do - to someone in order to avoid disaster. Starks quickly come to realize that he isn't the first person on Mr. R's radar of revenge.<br /><br />This was real nail biter. Starks is perhaps not the most likeable of characters, but he doesn't deserve the cruel game devised for him, so I quickly began to root for him. I had no clue about anything and the ending took me rather my surprise. Recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5332853473489511713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2230613109" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2230613109" />
    <a title="Victoria Castillo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49501590-victoria-castillo"><img alt="Victoria Castillo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504826942p2/49501590.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2230613109?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria Castillo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria Castillo" href="/user/show/49501590-victoria-castillo">Victoria Castillo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49501590-victoria-castillo?shelf=got-me-on-the-edge-of-my-seat">got-me-on-the-edge-of-my-seat</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49501590-victoria-castillo?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49501590-victoria-castillo?shelf=brain-burner">brain-burner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49501590-victoria-castillo?shelf=what-the-fuck">what-the-fuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49501590-victoria-castillo?shelf=slow-as-shit">slow-as-shit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2230613109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7724679008577827204">This book was not only slow as shit, it was also kinda heavy, but i'm sick, and i'm on my red days, and i'm on vacation so i had plenty of time and nothing to do except for swallowing some good books.<br/><br/>A friend of mine bought this, and she devour it in mere days, so of course, she recommended it to me. And after reading that blurb, i knew this had to be one of my first ones this year.<br/><br/>(Sighs)<br/><br/>There's a lot to say about this book, but my head kinda hurts after that so i'll keep it short. <br/><br/>Dr Frederick</span>
  <span id="freeText7724679008577827204" style="display:none">This book was not only slow as shit, it was also kinda heavy, but i'm sick, and i'm on my red days, and i'm on vacation so i had plenty of time and nothing to do except for swallowing some good books.<br /><br />A friend of mine bought this, and she devour it in mere days, so of course, she recommended it to me. And after reading that blurb, i knew this had to be one of my first ones this year.<br /><br />(Sighs)<br /><br />There's a lot to say about this book, but my head kinda hurts after that so i'll keep it short. <br /><br />Dr Frederick Starks is a regular, common man. He has a good job in a career he enjoys, and his life is a very boring routine. Then, on the day of his birthday, he recieves a letter that changes everything.<br /><br /><blockquote> <b>"Happy fifty-third birthday, Doctor. Welcome to the first day of your death. You ruined my life. And now I fully intend to ruin yours." </b> </blockquote><br /><br />The reader accompanies the protagonist along in a wild, desperate journey to saves his life, one full of secrets, revelations and discoveries, both personal and about the man who tortures him.<br /><br />I had never read a novel so deeply woven with the subject of psychology, and I must say that I found it deeply fascinating. Yes, this book drags a little. At the first half of it, they were parts when i wanted to skip some pages to reach the revelations, but once i got past the 50% mark or so, i just coudn't put it down. <br /><br />Somehow, John manages to keep the reader on the edge of the seat, to weave all the plots and subplots masterfully, to give you enough to keep reading, but not enough to make the book predictable, or give you away the ending. <br /><br />The side characters are masterfully done too. A first, they appear to be one-dimmensional, they are there just to "help" the protagonist with his mission,and even then, they are enchantic, and amazing and scary, but then you get to meet them, thorugh Frederick's eyes, and part of their stories too, and suddenly this people who where covered with mist and wonder and danger are now mere mortals, and the emotion to read that change was incredible, at least for me. <br /><br />Frederick's journey was very well written as well. We read how he goes from being a simple man, in the middle of his fifties, to a worthy opponent in this strange game of chess.<br /><br />I came to feel as deeply engaged and committed in the plot as the protagonist himself. I got to sympathize with his situation, I was distressed when he got anxious, angry when he got angry, and throughout the whole book, i was desperate to reach the end.<br /><br />The end was amazing too. Without a shadow of doubt, the best part of the book. It kept me biting my nails at four a.M, reading despise my sleepiness and my headache, and when it was over, I ended up lying in my bed, with insomnia, mentally reviewing the entire book, unable to believe what had happened, impressed with the way things had ended. I could never have imagined that they would be that way, or WHO was going to be the one behind everything ... I had to read it several times to make sure it was real, I never would have expected it.<br /><br />Anyway, without a doubt a great way to start the new year, with a great book. The only reason I did not give this five stars was because it was difficult for me to get through the first half of the book, and in some places I wanted to skip pages. Still, it was worth it.<br /><br />Definitely recommended!<br /><br />As always, I'm sorry for grammar and spelling errors</span>
  <a data-text-id="7724679008577827204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3331284082" />
    <a title="Josy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24848249-josy"><img alt="Josy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452241150p2/24848249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3331284082?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josy" href="/user/show/24848249-josy">Josy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3331284082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4397502110875808581">Actually 3.5. <br/>This novel is packed full of action. Something is happening on every page, every moment. It's truly a ride. The prose is good, it flows. Although some parts of the book do drag, most of them are quite a quick read. I believe the book as a whole is a little too long, but it's definitely readable. <br/>I didn't particularly like the main character, however. To me, he was rather useless for the whole first half of the book, before he did a complete 180 and reinvented himself in the second </span>
  <span id="freeText4397502110875808581" style="display:none">Actually 3.5. <br />This novel is packed full of action. Something is happening on every page, every moment. It's truly a ride. The prose is good, it flows. Although some parts of the book do drag, most of them are quite a quick read. I believe the book as a whole is a little too long, but it's definitely readable. <br />I didn't particularly like the main character, however. To me, he was rather useless for the whole first half of the book, before he did a complete 180 and reinvented himself in the second part (something that was a little unbelievable). In the second, he was a bit too arrogant. I understand he is an analyst, but I didn't appreciate his never ending inner-monologues of how he thought his rivals were thinking, what they were doing. Sometimes, his stream of consciousness bordered on omniscient narration, and it was a slip I didn't particularly appreciate or understand. <br />The ending was also not as satisfactory as I would've liked. Too many revelations and truths were based on pure coincidence or on elements that the reader could not possibly have been privy to. His final confrontation was also rather anti-climatic, something which, after having awaited it for 480 pages, seems rather irking. <br />All in all, the dread and paranoia were well portrayed, and I enjoyed it overall.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4397502110875808581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53614356-michael-adamchuk?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3092762175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3703360662397523671">Frederick Stark, a 53 yo psychiatrist gets a letter from Rumplestiltskin. It tells Starks that he must identify who Rumplestiltskin is within 15 days. If he doesn't, he must either commit suicide or one of his friends or relatives will be harmed. A fast paced novel from here on in as Stark goes through his past patients, figures out who Rumplestiltskin is and the tries to pull a fast one by staging his death. Stark then adopts different personna in his quest to finish off Rumplestiltskin. Good s</span>
  <span id="freeText3703360662397523671" style="display:none">Frederick Stark, a 53 yo psychiatrist gets a letter from Rumplestiltskin. It tells Starks that he must identify who Rumplestiltskin is within 15 days. If he doesn't, he must either commit suicide or one of his friends or relatives will be harmed. A fast paced novel from here on in as Stark goes through his past patients, figures out who Rumplestiltskin is and the tries to pull a fast one by staging his death. Stark then adopts different personna in his quest to finish off Rumplestiltskin. Good story and plotting.</span>

<div id="review_1592026973" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1592026973" />
    <a title="Tomàs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53725187-tom-s"><img alt="Tomàs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457985462p2/53725187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1592026973?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tomàs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tomàs" href="/user/show/53725187-tom-s">Tomàs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53725187-tom-s?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53725187-tom-s?shelf=mine">mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53725187-tom-s?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53725187-tom-s?shelf=in-spanish">in-spanish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1592026973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1514318252571542465">I've been thinking what I could write to describe as accurately as possible the book. I like to read good reviews which are able to change my mind and make me read a book when it's good. But I'm sorry to say I can't even do that. <br/><br/>The book was..., terrific. One of the best I read this year so far, and maybe one of the best that I've ever read in my life. And I'm not exaggerating. <br/><br/>The <b>plot</b> was well-thought and well-developed, in every aspect of the book. Divided in three part, each of them centred</span>
  <span id="freeText1514318252571542465" style="display:none">I've been thinking what I could write to describe as accurately as possible the book. I like to read good reviews which are able to change my mind and make me read a book when it's good. But I'm sorry to say I can't even do that. <br><br>The book was..., terrific. One of the best I read this year so far, and maybe one of the best that I've ever read in my life. And I'm not exaggerating. <br><br>The <b>plot</b> was well-thought and well-developed, in every aspect of the book. Divided in three part, each of them centred on an aspect of the book (I’m sorry but I won’t reveal anything. No spoilers in my reviews). And even though I read some reviews that suggested the second part was going to be slow and tedious. I completely disagree. I couldn’t stop reading it, without knowing what to expect next. It was surprise after surprise and I liked that a lot. <br><br>The moment the name of the antagonist was revealed I scream at the tops of my lungs “I knew it”. Agg! That made me so happy. Because really I didn’t know who the hell the “bad guy” was and when I found it…, it was great. <br><br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442018972ra/16182574.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>Then we have the <b>characters</b>. Can I say that I love <u>Ricky</u>, please? I know at the very first moment when you start knowing about him (I mean he is the main character, so that would be in the first page) I thought I would hate him (maybe he’s more similar to me that I would like to consider) but whilst I was reading and things were happening, he evolved. And that’s a very important aspect in every character for me. They need to be relatable if you want me to like a book. So when with every change and plot-twist in the novel he made a decision that in some aspect I could identify to (if I was in that situation, obviously), it made him more likeable, in some strange sense. And I like that, a lot. <br><br>And then we have Virgil, Rumpelstiltskin and Merlin. I won’t say many things about <u>Merlin</u>. He was necessary, but I didn’t like him. I’m sorry. But, but, but, the other two were like the best thing John Katzenbach could have ever done with this book. Mainly due to <u>Rumpelstiltskin</u> being the one who sent the letter to Ricky at the start of the novel. But the true antagonist was and will always be <u>Virgil</u>. His guide to hell. She was a really interesting character and I enjoyed the way she acted in front of Ricky. <br><br>*I’m sorry if there’s any inaccuracy, but the version I read was the Spanish one, so…<br><br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460037013ra/18690043.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>And well, that’s more or less what I wanted to say. Anyway, I recommend it to all of you. I’m sure you will like it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1514318252571542465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('p6QNombaBTzMfi/Rjx47hQdRlxocDfzRtbn9HBYPSHedgmRw3YTMVGtVm7B46zFa0Q5w0tKAcrbux7ut20y67Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FHxvyYU+cX/kXoOjumXjC5/bQaMfurKI6XS/SsRJRwIuWgYbPmC4F0N1N8JNkOnUSYSma9E3PO+yCvn7CQq1mA==')})
  }

Para quien todavía no la leyó, El túnel es la mejor introducción al univ<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText9170310331661814268\" style=\"display:none\">Breve e intensa novela publicada en 1948, este logrado fruto de la denominada &quot;literatura existencial&quot; le dio a su autor un reconocimiento que traspasó las fronteras nacionales. Para quien todavía no la leyó, El túnel es la mejor introducción al universo prodigioso de Ernesto Sábato; para quien la conoce, un clásico de las letras del continente, una historia sobre el drama del hombre arrojado en el sinsentido más doloroso: la conciencia de la nada. \nEl narrador describe una historia de amor y muerte en la que muestra la soledad del individuo contemporáneo. No están ausentes de esta trama policial y de suspenso, la locura y la increíble reflexión del protagonista, el pintor Juan Pablo Castel, debatiéndose por comprender las causas que lo arrastraron a matar a la mujer que amaba, María Iribarne, y que era su única vía de salvación. En este alucinante drama de la vida interior, seres intrincados en la bestial búsqueda de comprensión ceden a la mentira, la hipocresía y los celos desmedidos hasta el crimen más inexplicable. Aventura amorosa, aventura onírica, aventura del ser que dan testimonio de un asesinato, de cierta memoria culpable y de una valiente introspección. \nTécnicamente perfecta y de lectura apasionante, El túnel excede el negativismo ácido de Sartre y la frenética huida hacia el vacío que plantea El extranjero de Camus, pero tiene de esos dos maestros literarios la impronta genial que hace de la escritura una radiografía del alma atormentada.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"9170310331661814268\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n Le délai est près d’expirer quand soudain tout bascule pour lui : son ami et ancien professeur d’université, Harry Quebert, l’un des écrivains les plus respectés du pays, est rattrapé par son passé et se retrouve accusé d’avoir assassiné, en 1975, Nola Kellergan, une jeune fille de 15 ans, avec qui il aurait eu une liaison. Convaincu de l’innocence de Harry, Marcus abandonne tout pour se rendre dans le New Hampshire et mener son enquête. Il est rapidement dépassé par les événements : l’enquête s’enfonce et il fait l’objet de menaces. Pour innocenter Harry et sauver sa carrière d’écrivain, il doit absolument répondre à trois questions : Qui a tué Nola Kellergan? Que s’est-il passé dans le New Hampshire à l’été 1975? <span id="freeTextContainer1477030761289674695">John Katzenbach is a U.S. author of popular fiction. Son of Nicholas Katzenbach, former United States Attorney General, John worked as a criminal court reporter for the Miami Herald and Miami News, and a featured writer for the Herald’s Tropic magazine. He is married to Madeleine Blais and they live in western Massachusetts.<br/><br/>He left the newspaper grind to write books, racking up 12 novels so far, p</span>
  <span id="freeText1477030761289674695" style="display:none">John Katzenbach is a U.S. author of popular fiction. Son of Nicholas Katzenbach, former United States Attorney General, John worked as a criminal court reporter for the Miami Herald and Miami News, and a featured writer for the Herald’s Tropic magazine. He is married to Madeleine Blais and they live in western Massachusetts.<br /><br />He left the newspaper grind to write books, racking up 12 novels so far, psychological thrillers that have made him an international success. His first, 1982's bestselling *In the Heat of the Summer, became the movie *The Mean Season , filmed partially in The Herald's newsroom ans starring Kurt Russell and MAriel Hemingway.<br /><br />Two more of his books were made into films in the United States, 1995's *Just Cause and 2002's *Hart's War. A fourth book, *The Wrong Man was recently made into the soon-to-be-released French film Faux Coupable.</span>
